  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_02c29897-4861-40b3-890d-031b65c9f3bf'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer9398653297781168807">She soars above a world of warriors, kings, and priests. The daughter of Belgarath and the shape-shifter Poledra, she has fought wars, plotted palace coups, and worked her powerful magic for three thousand years.   <span id="freeText9398653297781168807" style="display:none">She soars above a world of warriors, kings, and priests. The daughter of Belgarath and the shape-shifter Poledra, she has fought wars, plotted palace coups, and worked her powerful magic for three thousand years. Now, Polgara looks back at her magnificent life, in this fitting crown jewel to the saga that is the Eddings' Belgariad and Mallorean cycles. <br /><br />Her hair streaked white by her father's first touch, her mind guided by a mother she will not see again for centuries, Polgara begins life in her Uncle Beldin's tower, and in the prehistorical, magical Tree that stands in the middle of the Vale. There, she first learns the reaches of her powers. There she assumes the bird shapes that will serve her on her adventures. And there she starts on the path toward her destiny as Duchess of Erat, shepherdess of the cause of good, adversary of Torak the One-Eyed Dragon God, and guardian of the world's last, best hope: the heir to the Rivan throne.<br /><br />Here is the legendary life story of a woman of wit, passion, and complex emotions, a woman born of two majestic parents who could not have been more unlike one another. Ordained to make peace and make war, to gain love and lose love, Polgara lives out her family's rich prophecy in the ceaseless struggle between the Light and the Dark.<br /><br />Polgara is the epic culmination of a magnificent saga, and a fitting farewell to a world which, once experienced, will never be forgotten.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9398653297781168807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/1779645-can-this-be-read-as-a-stand-alone-my">Can this be read as a stand-alone? My library only has this one book by David Eddings.</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3810595-katie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1577776261i/3810595._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3810595-katie">Katie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I just listened to this on Audible because it happened to be 2-for-1, having never read anything by this author before. I loved it! I think, however, <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I just listened to this on Audible because it happened to be 2-for-1, having never read anything by this author before. I loved it! I think, however, at times I kept thinking it would have been better if I'd read the Belgareth one first, as the narrator refers to it quite a lot! There's a big piece of the plot that I don't quite understand, and it almost fizzles out at the end, because I think the narrator assumes prior knowledge! That said, I still gave it four stars and I absolutely loved it, even though it's not at all the kind of thing I usually read. I usually struggle with anything over 400 pages. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_63144993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63144993" />
    <a title="Jeremy Preacher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1973239-jeremy-preacher"><img alt="Jeremy Preacher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379094189p2/1973239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63144993?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeremy Preacher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeremy Preacher" href="/user/show/1973239-jeremy-preacher">Jeremy Preacher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345416629" href="/book/show/1018296.Polgara_the_Sorceress">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1973239-jeremy-preacher?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63144993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13028813780928532904">Oh, Polgara. Ten books of characterization completely undercut in this explosion of sexist twaddle. Depressingly, I think it's a better book in a lot of ways than Belgarath the Sorcerer - the material is largely new (and entertaining) and, with the exception of the almost word-for-word repeat of the Vo Mimbre section, is paced fairly well. But it's got two big problems that I can't overlook.<br/><br/>The sexism. This is the Eddings' chance to expound at appalling length their various opinions about the ha</span>
  <span id="freeText13028813780928532904" style="display:none">Oh, Polgara. Ten books of characterization completely undercut in this explosion of sexist twaddle. Depressingly, I think it's a better book in a lot of ways than Belgarath the Sorcerer - the material is largely new (and entertaining) and, with the exception of the almost word-for-word repeat of the Vo Mimbre section, is paced fairly well. But it's got two big problems that I can't overlook.<br /><br />The sexism. This is the Eddings' chance to expound at appalling length their various opinions about the hard-wired differences between men and women, leading women to be conniving, emotional, good in the kitchen and with children, completely irrational in love, and made for making babies. Now, in their defense, this does not (in any of their books) prevent women from doing all sorts of interesting and significant things, but good god this pernicious 1960s thinking makes me flinch away from the page about every fourth paragraph.<br /><br />The voice. This would have been the perfect opportunity to really develop Polgara's distinct voice - she's something of a restrained and mysterious figure throughout the books-with-plots, and her perspective should be unique. Instead, she sounds exactly like Belgarath throughout. Her audience-directed asides are even more irritating, if possible, but that's about the only distinguishing factor - except, of course, the frequent remarks about the differences between men and women.<br /><br />Not a book I would recommend to anyone, really. The amusing Arendish political escapades do not make up for the serious commitment to eyerolling required.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13028813780928532904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20722184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20722184" />
    <a title="Shira Karp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6049-shira-karp"><img alt="Shira Karp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227748313p2/6049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20722184?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2008</a>

  <span id="freeText3437467469403939286" style="display:none">An amazing companion to Belgarath the Sorcerer. Fills in all the blank spots. Would have been the perfect ending to the series had he just not opened up the speculations about who Wolf really is at the end, but I guess nothings perfect. Especially since there ain't no more Garion stories coming to clear that up. That upset me quite a bit. But other than that the book was excellent. When I first started reading the Belgariad I thought Polgara was extremely dry and I couldn't understand everyone's affection for her, she just didn't seem like the mothering type of figure to me that they were portraying her as. Of course, by the end of th Belgariad I'd come around, but THIS book really explains so much more about Polgara and why she is the way she is, I really fell in love with it.</span>

<div id="review_471425035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471425035" />
    <a title="L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6463881-l"><img alt="L" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/471425035?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L" href="/user/show/6463881-l">L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780246138446" href="/book/show/983162.Polgara_the_Sorceress">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer471425035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8698485346860813108">A magnificent epic fantasy novel that is an absorbing read, which combines a complex plot with remarkable imagination. <br/><br/> <br/>David and Leigh Eddings have triumphed again with this spectacular novel, to add to your collection of original fantasy works by masterful writers. No one can compare within modern fantasy writing like Eddings, whose distinctive style and unique flair is second to none and which is at the top with all the greatest writers of this genre. Having delighted in his various series’ ‘</span>
  <span id="freeText8698485346860813108" style="display:none">A magnificent epic fantasy novel that is an absorbing read, which combines a complex plot with remarkable imagination. <br /><br /> <br />David and Leigh Eddings have triumphed again with this spectacular novel, to add to your collection of original fantasy works by masterful writers. No one can compare within modern fantasy writing like Eddings, whose distinctive style and unique flair is second to none and which is at the top with all the greatest writers of this genre. Having delighted in his various series’ ‘the Belgariad’ and ‘the malloreon’ together with trilogies such as ‘the elenium’ and ‘the Tamuli’ this novel was one that I was really looking forward to reading, as it is the prequel to the Belgariad. This is the story of the Queen of truth, love, rage and destiny and which within the first few pages will take you on the most astonishing fantastical journey into the vale of Aldur. <br /><br />Polgara is not only a Sorceress but who chose a very different life for herself than the expected one, as she chose love for Durnik over money and material luxury. A busy mother and wife who lives on a farm Polgara’s life is simple until during the dead of winter her Nephew, the Rivan King Garion and his wife Ce’Nedra visit. Ce’Nadra’s son Geran will one day be king and so she sets her mind to it that the Sorcerer must reveal all to them, for instance her years at Vo Wacune or what happened to her at Gar or Nadrack. Evil is rising once more from the city of endless night and as the truth is disclosed the story of Wizardry and politics, doom and evil, love and magic are brought into the light. But as darkness falls so will too the luck and love that Polgara possess which have up until now saved the world…<br /><br />This has to be the crowning achievement of the greatest fantasy epic ever, where once again David and Leigh display the scope of imagination, humor and sheer depth of storytelling power which has made this series so popular for fantasy lovers in modern times. I still have the 1997 edition of this book which although considered ‘old’ now stands quite comfortably beside current authors such as Gail Z Martin and Patrick Rothfuss. This is a fantastic read and so I have to give it…<br /><br />4 ½ stars – not quite 5 as I do have a favorite amongst his books and this one is not it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8698485346860813108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7700211714635813941">This is a great addition to the story told with Polgara's usual dry wit, cutting sarcasm and superb observations.   <span id="freeText7700211714635813941" style="display:none">This is a great addition to the story told with Polgara's usual dry wit, cutting sarcasm and superb observations. This kind of follows/accompanies Belgarath the Sorcerer as some of the events overlap but instead of the calm laid back view of Belgarath we are treated to the more blunt to the point view of Polgara. Again it has the feel of fireside story telling, although since it is Pol it should be more of stove side story telling given her love of cooking and her need to feed people (I swear she has some Welsh blood in her!). As with Belgarath, there is plenty of action as well as the more human aspects of the story to keep things ticking over and plenty of the behind the scenes stuff that the main series has missed.</span>

<div id="review_375442974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/375442974" />
    <a title="Jade Kerrion" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10431470-jade-kerrion"><img alt="Jade Kerrion" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340480072p2/10431470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/375442974?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jade Kerrion" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jade Kerrion" href="/user/show/10431470-jade-kerrion">Jade Kerrion</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375442974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15739610662158741754">"Polgara the Sorceress" wraps up David Eddings's high fantasy series that started with the 5 books of the Belgariad, continued through the 5 books of the Mallorean, and "Belgarath the Sorceror." Eddings cleverly precludes complaints of inconsistencies between "Belgarath" and "Polgara" by having Polgara say that people remember things differently.<br/><br/>By the last book in the series, Eddings's easy style and insider jokes settles on readers like a comfortable and worn cloak. The characters welcome you </span>
  <span id="freeText15739610662158741754" style="display:none">"Polgara the Sorceress" wraps up David Eddings's high fantasy series that started with the 5 books of the Belgariad, continued through the 5 books of the Mallorean, and "Belgarath the Sorceror." Eddings cleverly precludes complaints of inconsistencies between "Belgarath" and "Polgara" by having Polgara say that people remember things differently.<br /><br />By the last book in the series, Eddings's easy style and insider jokes settles on readers like a comfortable and worn cloak. The characters welcome you like old friends,because by now, they really are like old friends. Stereotypes and archetypes abound, and there are few surprises in the novel. That said, "Polgara the Sorceress" is a fundamental read for any Eddings fan, especially for those who crave a sense of completion. The novel rounds out Belgarath's story and adds depth and nuance to major historical events.<br /><br />It is a fantastic end to the series, a story about a magnificent woman whose dedication to protecting the line of the Godslayer didn't preclude her from dabbling in politics, planning assassinations, overthrowing duchies, establishing kingdoms, dancing sensually enough to make jaws drop, and having a whale of a time while doing so. Now, that is a life worth living.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15739610662158741754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_294107692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/294107692" />
    <a title="Simon Mcleish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7915393-simon-mcleish"><img alt="Simon Mcleish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347099463p2/7915393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/294107692?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon Mcleish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon Mcleish" href="/user/show/7915393-simon-mcleish">Simon Mcleish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294107692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15011554655545775058">Originally published on my blog <a href='http://simonsbookblog.blogspot.com/1998/09/david-leigh-eddings-polgara-sorceress.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> in September 1998.<br/><br/>Polgara the Sorceress is the second prequel to the Belgariad and Malloreon series. The different author attribution of this and Belgarath the Sorcerer apparently reflects not a change in how David Eddings' books are written, but is more an overdue acknowledgement. The story of the world of Belgarath and his family now occupies twelve books, though the two prequels match in length any two of the others.<br/><br/>The first prequel tells a first person n</span>
  <span id="freeText15011554655545775058" style="display:none">Originally published on my blog <a href="http://simonsbookblog.blogspot.com/1998/09/david-leigh-eddings-polgara-sorceress.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> in September 1998.<br /><br />Polgara the Sorceress is the second prequel to the Belgariad and Malloreon series. The different author attribution of this and Belgarath the Sorcerer apparently reflects not a change in how David Eddings' books are written, but is more an overdue acknowledgement. The story of the world of Belgarath and his family now occupies twelve books, though the two prequels match in length any two of the others.<br /><br />The first prequel tells a first person narrative of the life of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/189802.Belgarath_the_Sorcerer" title="Belgarath the Sorcerer by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Belgarath the Sorcerer</a>, 'the Eternal Man'; this second one is the same, courtesy of his daughter, Polgara. There is naturally some overlap (as Belgarath has been alive through the whole of his daughter's life), but they concentrate on different aspects of the history of the Eddings' world.<br /><br />Even though they come first chronologically, the prequels would not be a very interesting read before the remainder of the series. The place to start is with the first volume of the Belgariad, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44659.Pawn_of_Prophecy__The_Belgariad___1_" title="Pawn of Prophecy (The Belgariad, #1) by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Pawn of Prophecy</a> (which was published first). If you enjoy that series and the Malloreon, then come back to the two prequels. (Their scene-setting introductions follow on after the end of the main series.)<br /><br />Myself, I would be pleased to see the Eddings abandon the arch tone that they take in the whole series, and which is particularly annoying in the prequels. There is a distinct sentimental vein to David Eddings - I once read an interview in which he referred to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5493564.Tolkien_J__R__R_" title="Tolkien J. R. R." rel="nofollow noopener">Tolkien J. R. R.</a> rather nauseatingly as "Papa" - but he is able to jettison it when he desires to do so. His contemporary novels, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110691.High_Hunt" title="High Hunt by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">High Hunt</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110689.The_Losers" title="The Losers by David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Losers</a>, are much better written because in them he assumes a rather different style which works well. To sum up, Polgara the Sorceress is probably for fans only.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15011554655545775058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1293701449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1293701449" />
    <a title="Maddy Lanslots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42625743-maddy-lanslots"><img alt="Maddy Lanslots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430330265p2/42625743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1293701449?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddy Lanslots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddy Lanslots" href="/user/show/42625743-maddy-lanslots">Maddy Lanslots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1293701449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5649583868426074228">4,5*<br/><br/>What a wonderful book!<br/>It's taken me a while to pick it up, but after re-reading the BELGARIAD and MALLOREON series for the third (fourth?) time, I decided I wanted to read its two companion pieces as well. I started with POLGARA and... wow. It's been an incredible ride. I thought I wouldn't like this book as much as I do the original series, because it doesn't have all the characters I've come to know and love (aside from Polgara, Belgarath, and a handful of others). I found myself falling i</span>
  <span id="freeText5649583868426074228" style="display:none">4,5*<br /><br />What a wonderful book!<br />It's taken me a while to pick it up, but after re-reading the BELGARIAD and MALLOREON series for the third (fourth?) time, I decided I wanted to read its two companion pieces as well. I started with POLGARA and... wow. It's been an incredible ride. I thought I wouldn't like this book as much as I do the original series, because it doesn't have all the characters I've come to know and love (aside from Polgara, Belgarath, and a handful of others). I found myself falling in love with all the new characters throughout the story, however.<br /><br />Polgara's story is a long and complicated one, starting in her mother's womb before she and Beldaran are even born. It tells of her relationship with her mother and her twin sister, the animosity she feels towards her father and her ongoing relationship with him, the way she finally loses Beldaran (multiple times, in several ways), and the way she learns about her gift and how to use it. Her time in Arendia is covered thoroughly and I loved reading about her time in Vo Wacune, keeping the Arends in check, and being the Duchess of Erat. The story is told in such a way that I could almost feel my heart break every time something terrible happened, showing how awful it can really be to have a lifespan as long as Polgara's.<br />Of course, the fact that she watches over the Rivan line - her sister's line - is also an important plot element. We find out what it was like for Polgara to raise so many little boys, to keep them hidden and take care of them as she waited for the Godslayer to be born. The final part, leading up to Garion's birth and briefly afterwards, was beautiful and so sad at the same time. So many bad things happen in Polgara's story, but there are also so many wonderful things.<br /><br />I really felt myself drawn into this story and although it dragged ever so slightly a couple of times, it was never for long. It's quite action-packed, in a way, so each time I started feeling like nothing much was happening, something did happen that had me on the edge of my seat again. A beautiful companion read to the BELGARIAD and the MALLOREON. I'll be picking up Belgarath's story next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5649583868426074228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715282958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer250155746257763816">This book held my interest more than Belgarath the Sorcerer, but again was marred by inconsistencies. The character interactions are unfortunately quite repetitive and the characterisation of women is not very nuanced. On reflection, I probably shouldn't have tried to re-read of ALL of the Belgariad world books haha. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16440981783964431248">4 Stars<br/><br/>Polgara the Sorceress by David Eddings is the amazing companion book to Belgraith the Sorcerer. Another epic fantasy from the clever imagination of Mr. Eddings this story is well worth the read for any fantasy lover.<br/>We met Polgara back in The Belgariad Series, and I have to admit that at first I really didn’t like her much at all.   <span id="freeText16440981783964431248" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />Polgara the Sorceress by David Eddings is the amazing companion book to Belgraith the Sorcerer. Another epic fantasy from the clever imagination of Mr. Eddings this story is well worth the read for any fantasy lover.<br />We met Polgara back in The Belgariad Series, and I have to admit that at first I really didn’t like her much at all. But slowly , over time, I began to understand her more and by the end of that series I didn’t think she was as annoying as I had first thought. <br />In this book we get a lot more background information, and learn things that weren’t revealed in earlier books. This story really explains why/how she is the way she is. And she definitely won me over.<br />Another enthralling, well written story from Mr. Eddings.<br /><br />Happy Reading!<br /></span>

Even though I have some previous background knowledge of this epic, I just had to give up trying to sort out all the empires, kingdoms, princip</span>
  <span id="freeText9688433039710696145" style="display:none">It's a few years since I read the Belgariad, so I didn't immediately identify with the characters and it did take me a little while to become involved in the story. <br />Overall the characters are engaging although I had a bit of a love-hate relationship with Polgara. <br />The thing that really lets the book down is the over-complication of politics and of places. Even though I have some previous background knowledge of this epic, I just had to give up trying to sort out all the empires, kingdoms, principalities and duchies.<br />So it rates somewhere between a 3 and a 4 star for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9688433039710696145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8437079929525777998">It's been a while since I read the final, 12th book in the Belgariad by David and Leigh Eddings and it was a little emotional when putting down the book for the last time just now. <br/><br/>I don't care if the writing is simplified and was probably what would be called Young Adult now, I love these books and am so glad to have revisited them.</span>

<div id="review_20648302" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20648302" />
    <a title="Stacey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1065875-stacey"><img alt="Stacey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232913448p2/1065875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20648302?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey" href="/user/show/1065875-stacey">Stacey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1065875-stacey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20648302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13849823440607518303">I enjoyed the story of these books so much. I love the world that it is set in; it is so well developed (even if it is a bit static, no culture stays the same for 7000 years) and I appreciated getting Polgara's adventures that rounded out Belgarath's. I enjoyed all the time spend in Arendia & Sendaria, her run ins with various Salmissra's & Tolnedran emporers and all the time she spent raising generations of Rivan heirs.<br/>I do not enjoy her, and her mother's, rampant misandry. Men are all little b</span>
  <span id="freeText13849823440607518303" style="display:none">I enjoyed the story of these books so much. I love the world that it is set in; it is so well developed (even if it is a bit static, no culture stays the same for 7000 years) and I appreciated getting Polgara's adventures that rounded out Belgarath's. I enjoyed all the time spend in Arendia &amp; Sendaria, her run ins with various Salmissra's &amp; Tolnedran emporers and all the time she spent raising generations of Rivan heirs.<br />I do not enjoy her, and her mother's, rampant misandry. Men are all little boys that never grow up and have to be guided by the wiser and more mature women. I didn't enjoy it 20 years ago either but with the changes in culture we have experience in that time it's even harder sometimes to read. (see, and only 20 years have passed). I can ignore some of it but it's so constant and unrelenting. Its difficult to shrug off now. If a male character spoke about women the way Polgara spoke about men I wouldn't have finished the book 20 years ago. The endless misogyny would have driven me to throw the book in the trash.<br />Polgara is possibly the bossiest person I have ever encountered in fiction. She is supremely convinced of the rightness of her actions. She and she alone is the 'grown up' in the room and everyone else is under her thumb or else. Her terrorizing the Arendish dukes into doing what she says by basically torturing one of them with stomach ulcers is just an example.<br />But while I often dislike the main character (and never warm to Poledra), I do love the overall story this book is a part of and as with all my reading, I'm going to reread it for completeness every time.<br />I'll just be annoyed while I do it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13849823440607518303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('huu5NYkNpXZsxsEWOMOmb8krFrVsHMqYO0u+526U9tmOLeyuTRLWuA9KL5cQPolJPJ6T3XgW6ahefKye2Nj0/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('61Foq85xgZnGfWQSeyHEK/LHQ1Ekp40nRBdyWo6jlDTjlz0wCm7yV6XxipNT3OsNB3LGOTCtrhchIGAjOO+WEQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings">About David Eddings</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1223870462p3/8732.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings">David Eddings
</a></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11522192244742766925">David Eddings was an American author who wrote several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.Leigh_Eddings' title='Leigh Eddings' rel='nofollow noopener'>Leigh Eddings</a>
</b>, was an uncredited co-author on many of his early books, but he had later acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br/><br/>David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he a</span>
  <span id="freeText11522192244742766925" style="display:none">David Eddings was an American author who wrote several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.Leigh_Eddings" title="Leigh Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Eddings</a>
</b>, was an uncredited co-author on many of his early books, but he had later acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br /><br />David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he achieved great success. In a recent interview with sffworld.com, he said: "I don't take orders from readers."<br /><br />On January 26, 2007 it was reported that Eddings accidentally burned about a quarter of his office, next door to his house, along with his Excalibur sports car, and the original manuscripts for most of his novels. He was flushing the fuel tank of the car with water when he lit a piece of paper and threw into the puddle to test if it was still flammable.<br /><br />On February 28, 2007, David Eddings' wife, Leigh Eddings (born Judith Leigh Schall), died following a series of strokes. She was 69.<br /><br />David Eddings died on June 2, 2009 at the age of 77.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11522192244742766925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
